Source Code

These source-code files were derived originally from the scan from MIT's Dibner Institute's now-discontinued website titled "History of Recent Science and Technology". It is believed that the original listing was preserved by AGC developer Don Eyles, copied/reduced by AGC developer Hugh Blair-Smith, passed by AGC developer James Kernan to collector David Craig, scanned by Gary Neff, and then passed to the Dibner Institute where unfortunately the high-quality scans were reduced in legibility as part of the online-presentation process, and the original scans discarded. The source code was transcribed from those images by Ron Burkey. The images from the Dibner Institute website, and unfortunately not the discarded original high-quality scans, though with a few high-quality replacement scans provided directly by Gary Neff, are now available at the Virtual AGC project website. Report any conversion errors to info@sandroid.org. Notations on the program listing read, in part:

	GAP:  ASSEMBLE REVISION 131 OF AGC PROGRAM LUMINARY BY NASA 2021112-091
	17:53 DEC. 19, 1969
Note that the date is the date of the printout, not the date of the program revision. 

000002,000002:                                                                                                  #  Copyright:    Public domain.
000003,000003:                                                                                                  #  Filename:     MAIN.agc
000004,000004:                                                                                                  #  Purpose:      The main source file for Luminary 1C, revision 131.
000005,000005:                                                                                                  #                It is part of the source code for the Lunar Module's (LM)
000006,000006:                                                                                                  #                Apollo Guidance Computer (AGC) for Apollo 13 and Apollo 14.
000007,000007:                                                                                                  #  Assembler:    yaYUL
000008,000008:                                                                                                  #  Contact:      Ron Burkey <info@sandroid.org>.
000009,000009:                                                                                                  #  Website:      www.ibiblio.org/apollo/index.html
000010,000010:                                                                                                  #  Mod history:  04/12/03 RSB.   Began.
000011,000011:                                                                                                  #                05/05/03 RSB.   ...continued.
000012,000012:                                                                                                  #                05/11/03 RSB    Draft of this file completed.
000013,000013:                                                                                                  #                06/08/03 RSB    Drafts of all the included files completed.
000014,000014:                                                                                                  #                05/14/05 RSB    Corrected website reference above.
000015,000015:                                                                                                  #                06/30/09 RSB    Added an experimental HTML note.
000016,000016: 
000017,000017:                                                                                                  #  The contents of the "Luminary131" files, in general, are
000018,000018:                                                                                                  #  transcribed from a scanned document obtained from MIT's website, namely
000019,000019:                                                                                                  #  http://hrst.mit.edu/hrs/apollo/public/archive/1729.pdf.  Notations on this
000020,000020:                                                                                                  #  document read, in part:
000021,000021: 
000022,000022:                                                                                                  #        NASA Apollo LUMINARY 131 (1C) Program Source Code Listing.
000023,000023:                                                                                                  #        MIT Instrumentation/Draper Laboratory -- 19 December 1969, 1742 pages.
000024,000024:                                                                                                  #        This listing contains the flight program for the Lunar Module 
000025,000025:                                                                                                  #        as created by MIT's Draper Lab for the Apollo 13/14 moon missions.
000026,000026: 
000027,000027:                                                                                                  #  Refer directly to the online document mentioned above for further information.
000028,000028:                                                                                                  #  Please report any errors (relative to 1729.pdf) to info@sandroid.org.
000029,000029: 
000030,000030:                                                                                                  #  This file is a little different from the other Luminary131 files I'm providing, 
000031,000031:                                                                                                  #  in that it doesn't represent anything that appears directly in the original source.  
000032,000032:                                                                                                  #  What I (RSB) have done for organizational purposes is to split the huge monolithic
000033,000033:                                                                                                  #  source code into smaller, more manageable chunks--i.e., into individual source 
000034,000034:                                                                                                  #  files.  Those files are rejoined within this file as "includes".  It just makes
000035,000035:                                                                                                  #  it a little easier to work with.  The code chunks correspond to natural divisions
000036,000036:                                                                                                  #  into sub-programs.  In fact, these divisions are more-or-less specified by
000037,000037:                                                                                                  #  the source code itself.  Refer to the "TABLE OF SUBROUTINE LOG SECTIONS" at the
000038,000038:                                                                                                  #  very beginning of the file ASSEMBLY_AND_OPERATION_INFORMATION.agc.
000039,000039: 
000040,000040:                                                                                                  #  It may be reasonably asked why tens of thousands of lines of source are joined by
000041,000041:                                                                                                  #  means of inclusion, rather than simply assembling the source files individually and
000042,000042:                                                                                                  #  then linking them to form the executable.  The answer is that the original 
000043,000043:                                                                                                  #  development team had no linker.  The builds were monolithic just like this.
000044,000044:                                                                                                  #  There was a big emphasis on reusability of the code in the original project, 
000045,000045:                                                                                                  #  apparently, but this reusability took the form of inserting your deck of 
000046,000046:                                                                                                  #  punch-cards at the appropriate position in somebody else's deck of punch-cards.
000047,000047:                                                                                                  #  So, indeed, the method of file-inclusion is a very fair representation of the 
000048,000048:                                                                                                  #  methods used in the original development ... with the improvement, of course,
000049,000049:                                                                                                  #  that you no longer have to worry about dropping the card deck.  On the other hand, 
000050,000050:                                                                                                  #  I wasn't there at the time, so I may have no idea what I'm talking about.
000051,000051: 
000052,000052:                                                                                                  #  Finally, note that the original Apollo AGC assembler (called "YUL") is no longer 
000053,000053:                                                                                                  #  available (as far as I can tell).  The replacement assembler yaYUL accepts 
000054,000054:                                                                                                  #  a slightly different format for the source code from what YUL accepted, so the 
000055,000055:                                                                                                  #  source code has been targeted for assembly with yaYUL.
000056,000056: 
000057,000057:                                                                                                  #  What follows is simply a bunch of file-includes for the individual code chunks.
000058,000058:                                                                                                  #  I've marked the page numbers vs. the original scanned listing (1729.pdf) to 
000059,000059:                                                                                                  #  make proof-reading easier.  Besides, the scanned listing contains a lot of
000060,000060:                                                                                                  #  interesting tables (cross-referenced to page numbers) created by YUL, 
000061,000061:                                                                                                  #  but not duplicated by yaYUL, so it's still valuable even if the source-files
000062,000062:                                                                                                  #  listed below are in hand.  Notice, though, that the page number herein are those
000063,000063:                                                                                                  #  the scanned (PDF) file, and not those which are marked on the scanned pages
000064,000064:                                                                                                  #  themselves, so there is not an exact correspondence between YUL-generated
000065,000065:                                                                                                  #  page numbers appearing within tables and the page numbers marked in this source
000066,000066:                                                                                                  #  code.
000067,000067: 
000068,000068:                                                                                                  #  pp. 1-5 contain no code/comments.
